## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (nonlinear oscillations / classical mechanics)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t, which is the standard state-space form of (possibly forced/damped) nonlinear oscillators. Typical structures include linear and nonlinear restoring forces in x, linear/nonlinear damping in v, and periodic or parametric forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (SHO): dv_dt = c0 * x (undamped, unforced linear restoring force; sign absorbed in c0)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring plus linear viscous damping)
- Constant-force / bias term: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 (gravity offset, actuator bias, equilibrium shift)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic stiffness plus linear damping)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like damping proportional to v|v|)
- Nonlinear damping (Rayleigh form): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (amplitude-dependent damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator (negative damping at small |x|): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations; constants capture 1 - x^2 type behavior)
- Liénard-type oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x + c3 * x**2) * v (general position-dependent damping/drive)
- Pendulum equation (small-to-moderate angles): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (nonlinear restoring torque with linear damping)
- Periodic forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (externally driven oscillator)
- Multi-harmonic forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) + c4 * sin(c5 * t) (richer drive spectrum / phase effects)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric resonance)
- Nonlinear forced Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (canonical nonlinear forced vibration model)
- State-coupled nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (energy transfer or geometry-dependent damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd restoring-force symmetry (centered potential) → dv_dt dominated by odd functions of x (x, x**3, sin(c*x)); indicates symmetric oscillations about equilibrium.
- Hardening/softening stiffness → presence of x**3 term; frequency increases/decreases with amplitude depending on the sign embedded in its coefficient.
- Viscous dissipation → linear v term; yields exponential decay of energy in free response when combined with linear x restoring.
- Dry/friction-like or quadratic drag → terms like v*Abs(v) or Abs(v); produces faster decay at high speeds and non-sinusoidal transients.
- Self-excitation / limit cycles → position-dependent damping multiplying v, e.g., (c0 + c1 * x**2) * v with sign change across amplitudes (Van der Pol/Liénard behavior).
- External periodic drive → additive sin/cos terms in t; implies sustained oscillations and resonance peaks when drive frequency matches natural frequency.
- Parametric resonance → time-periodic coefficient multiplying x (or v), e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x; can cause instability tongues even without direct forcing.
- Energy-preserving vs dissipative structure → absence of v-dependent terms suggests conservative dynamics; inclusion of v terms indicates damping or active control.
- Nonlinear mode coupling signature → mixed terms like x*v, x**2*v, or x**2*v*Abs(v); suggests amplitude-dependent damping or geometric nonlinearities.

\[

\]
Rewrite into basis terms:
- \(v\) term: \(-0.7210044\,v -1.0373701\,v = -1.758374516949398\,v\)
- \(v^3\) term: \(+0.721004421988058\,v^3\)
- \(x\) term: \(-2.44077135428351\,x\)
- \(x|v|^{1/3}\) term: \(-2.44077135428351\cdot 0.0154128049692563\, x|v|^{1/3}\)

So GT is exactly a linear combination of the four monomials:
\[
A\,x + B\,v + C\,v^3 + D\,x|v|^{1/3}
\]
with fixed coefficients \(A,B,C,D\), and **no** constant offset and **no** \(t\)-dependence.

Therefore any candidate can match GT iff it can be reduced (by setting its free constants) to exactly those four terms with the same coefficients, and all extra terms (constants, trig/exp/log, extra powers, mixed \(vx\), etc.) can be made identically zero.

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:**
`-0.721004421988058*v*(1 - v**2) - 1.03737009496134*v - 2.44077135428351*x*(0.0154128049692563*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.721004*v + 0.721004*v**3 - 1.03737*v - 2.44077*x*0.015413*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 2.44077*x`
- `= -2.44077*x - 1.75837*v + 0.721004*v**3 - 0.037627*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`

So GT = `A*x + B*v + C*v**3 + D*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` where:
- A = -2.44077
- B = -1.75837
- C = 0.721004
- D = -0.037627

The GT has **no constant term** (no offset), **no t-dependence**, and consists exactly of the basis functions: `x`, `v`, `v**3`, `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`.

Now I'll check each candidate. The key question is: can extra terms be zeroed out by setting their coefficients to 0, and do the remaining terms match the GT basis functions?

For candidates with a constant term `c_k` (standalone), I can set it to 0.
For candidates with extra additive terms like `c*sin(...)`, `c*cos(...)`, `c*exp(...)`, `c*log(...)`, etc., I can set the coefficient `c` to 0 to eliminate them.

Let me systematically check:

**Candidates with exactly {x, v, v**3, x*Abs(v)**(1/3)} plus zero-able terms:**

- **Candidate 1**: Has `c2*sin(c3+c4*t) + c5 + c8*cos(c9*t)` — set c2=0, c5=0, c8=0. Remaining: `c0*x + c1*v + c6*v**3 + c7*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`. ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 4**: Has `c2 + c5*x + c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(c8*x+c9)` — set c2=0, c6=0, absorb c5*x into c0*x. ✓ **MATCH**
